## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and concentration A, which is the fundamental problem of determining rate laws in chemical kinetics. The rate law typically depends on concentration raised to some power (reaction order), but time-dependent terms may appear in complex or driven reaction systems.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions with equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (externally driven reaction)
- Consecutive reaction integrated: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (rate from consecutive mechanism)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative kinetics)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (general polynomial in concentration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate values (dA_dt < 0) for a reactant indicate consumption, suggesting terms like -k*A^n with positive k and n
- If dA_dt depends only on A and not on t explicitly, the system is autonomous and follows a standard rate law dA/dt = f(A)
- Sigmoidal concentration profiles over time suggest autocatalytic mechanisms with A*(1-A) type rate terms
- If the rate changes sign at certain concentrations, this indicates reversible reactions or equilibrium, suggesting terms like c0*A + c1 or c0*(A - A_eq)
- Rational functions of A (Michaelis-Menten form) arise when intermediate species are in quasi-steady-state approximation
- Multiple exponential time dependencies suggest consecutive or parallel reaction mechanisms with distinct rate constants
- Cubic or higher-order polynomial dependence on A can indicate oscillatory chemical systems (e.g., Oregonator, Brusselator)
- If dA_dt is proportional to A^n where n is non-integer, this may reflect fractal kinetics or heterogeneous reaction environments
